/// Provider for `query mir_borrowck`. Similar to `typeck`, this must\n115: /// only be called for typeck roots which will then borrowck all\n116: /// nested bodies as well.\n117: fn mir_borrowck(\n118:     tcx: TyCtxt<'_>,\n119:     def: LocalDefId,\n120: ) -> Result<&FxIndexMap<LocalDefId, ty::DefinitionSiteHiddenType<'_>>, ErrorGuaranteed> {\n121:     assert!(!tcx.is_typeck_child(def.to_def_id()));\n122:     let (input_body, _) = tcx.mir_promoted(def);\n123:     debug!(\"run query mir_borrowck: {}\", tcx.def_path_str(def));\n124: \n125:     let input_body: &Body<'_> = &input_body.borrow();\n126:     if let Some(guar) = input_body.tainted_by_errors {\n127:         debug!(\"Skipping borrowck because of tainted body\");\n128:         Err(guar)\n129:     } else if input_body.should_skip() {\n130:         debug!(\"Skipping borrowck because of injected body\");\n131:         let opaque_types = Default::default();\n132:         Ok(tcx.arena.alloc(opaque_types))\n133:     } else {\n134:         let mut root_cx = BorrowCheckRootCtxt::new(tcx, def, None);\n135:         root_cx.do_mir_borrowck();\n136:         root_cx.finalize()\n137:     }\n138: }\n139: \n140: /// Data propagated to the typeck parent by nested items.\n141: /// This should always be empty for the typeck root.\n142: #[derive(Debug)]\n143: struct PropagatedBorrowCheckResults<'tcx> {\n144:     closure_requirements: Option<ClosureRegionRequirements<'tcx>>,\n145:     used_mut_upvars: SmallVec<[FieldIdx; 8]>,\n146: }\n147: \n148: type DeferredClosureRequirements<'tcx> = Vec<(LocalDefId, ty::GenericArgsRef<'tcx>, Locations)>;\n149: \n150: /// After we borrow check a closure, we are left with various\n151: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/lib.rs%3FL1-150"}}}

The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \\\"root\\\" of the\\n2: //! borrow forwards, iterating over \\\"similar\\\" projections in lockstep until\\n3: //! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\\n4: //! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\\n5: //!\\n6: //! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\\n7: //! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\\n8: //!\\n9: //! For example, if we are comparing these:\\n10: //! ```text\\n11: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n12: //! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\\n13: //! ```\\n14: //!\\n15: //! Then our steps are:\\n16: //! ```text\\n17: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n18: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n19: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n20: //!      *x1[2].y    |  *x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n21: //!     (*x1[2].y).z | (*x1[i].y).w  -- we are disjoint and don't need to check more!\\n22: //! ```\\n23: //!\\n24: //! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\\n25: //! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\\n26: //!\\n27: //! ```text\\n28: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n29: //! ACCESS:  x1[i].y\\n30: //! ```\\n31: //!\\n32: //! Then our steps are:\\n33: //! ```text\\n34: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n35: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n36: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n37: //! ```\\n38: //!\\n39: //! -- here we run out of access - the borrow can access a part of it. If this\\n40: //! is a full deep access, then we *know* the borrow conflicts with it. However,\\n41: //! if the access is shallow, then we can proceed:\\n42: //!\\n43: //! ```text\\n44: //!       x1[2].y    | (*x1[i].y)    -- a deref! the access can't get past this, so we\\n45: //!                                     are disjoint\\n46: //! ```\\n47: //!\\n48: //! Our invariant is, that at each step of the iteration:\\n49: //!  - If we didn't run out of access to match, our borrow and access are comparable\\n50: //!    and either equal or disjoint.\\n51: //!  - If we did run out of access, the borrow can access a part of it.\\n52: \\n53: use std::cmp::max;\\n54: use std::iter;\\n55: \\n56: use rustc_hir as hir;\\n57: use rustc_middle::bug;\\n58: use to influence decisions\\n67: /// where a place might be equal or disjoint with another place, such as if `a[i] == a[j]`.\\n68: /// `PlaceConflictBias::Overlap` would bias toward assuming that `i` might equal `j` and that these\\n69: /// places overlap. `PlaceConflictBias::NoOverlap` assumes that for the purposes of the predicate\\n70: /// being run in the calling context, the conservative
